<p><b>Sanford "Sandy" Koufax</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/oʊ/ long 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="'f' in 'find'">f</span><span title="/æ/ short 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span></span>/</a></span></span>; born <b>Sanford Braun</b>; December 30, 1935) is a former American <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> (MLB) left-handed <a href="/wiki/Pitcher" title="Pitcher">pitcher</a>. He pitched 12 seasons for the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Brooklyn/Los Angeles Dodgers</a>, from 1955 to 1966. Koufax, at age 36 in 1972, became the youngest player ever elected to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baseball_Hall_of_Fame" title="Baseball Hall of Fame">Baseball Hall of Fame</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kirbypuckett_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-kirbypuckett-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>Koufax's career peaked with a run of six outstanding years from <a href="/wiki/1961_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1961 Major League Baseball season">1961</a> to <a href="/wiki/1966_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1966 Major League Baseball season">1966</a>, before arthritis in his left elbow ended his career prematurely at age 30. He was an <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="Major League Baseball All-Star Game">All-Star</a> for six seasons<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-baseballhall.org_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-baseballhall.org-2">[2]</a></sup> and was the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MLB_Most_Valuable_Player_award" title="MLB Most Valuable Player award">Most Valuable Player</a> in <a href="/wiki/1963_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1963 Major League Baseball season">1963</a>. He won three <a href="/wiki/Cy_Young_Award" title="Cy Young Award">Cy Young Awards</a> in 1963, <a href="/wiki/1965_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1965 Major League Baseball season">1965</a>, and 1966, by unanimous votes, making him the first three-time Cy Young winner in baseball history and the only one to win three times when one overall award was given for all of major league baseball instead of one award for each league. Koufax also won the NL <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Triple_Crown" title="Major League Baseball Triple Crown">Triple Crown</a> for pitchers those same three years by leading the NL in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Win_(baseball)" title="Win (baseball)">wins</a>, <a href="/wiki/Strikeout" title="Strikeout">strikeouts</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Earned_run_average" title="Earned run average">earned run average</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbref-skoufax_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbref-skoufax-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Koufax was the first major league pitcher to pitch four <a href="/wiki/No-hitter" title="No-hitter">no-hitters</a> and the eighth pitcher to pitch a <a href="/wiki/Perfect_game" title="Perfect game">perfect game</a> in baseball history. Despite his comparatively short career, Koufax's 2,396 career strikeouts ranked 7th in history as of his retirement, trailing only <a href="/wiki/Warren_Spahn" title="Warren Spahn">Warren Spahn</a> (2,583) among left-handers. Koufax, <a href="/wiki/Randy_Johnson" title="Randy Johnson">Randy Johnson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Mart%C3%ADnez" title="Pedro Martínez">Pedro Martínez</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Nolan_Ryan" title="Nolan Ryan">Nolan Ryan</a> are the only four pitchers elected to the Hall of Fame who had more strikeouts than innings pitched.</p>
<p>Koufax is also remembered as one of the outstanding <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jew" title="Jew">Jewish</a> athletes in American sports. His decision not to pitch Game 1 of the <a href="/wiki/1965_World_Series" title="1965 World Series">1965 World Series</a> because it fell on <a href="/wiki/Yom_Kippur" title="Yom Kippur">Yom Kippur</a> garnered national attention as an example of conflict between professional pressures and personal beliefs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yomkippur_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-yomkippur-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sandy_Koufax&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Koufax was born in <a href="/wiki/Brooklyn" title="Brooklyn">Brooklyn</a>, New York, to a Jewish family, and raised in <a href="/wiki/Borough_Park,_Brooklyn" title="Borough Park, Brooklyn">Borough Park</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jewishvirtuallibrary.org_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-jewishvirtuallibrary.org-8">[8]</a></sup> His parents, Evelyn (née Lichtenstein) and Jack Braun, divorced when he was three years old. His mother was remarried when he was nine, to Irving Koufax.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hickocksports.com_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-hickocksports.com-9">[9]</a></sup> Shortly after his mother's remarriage, the family moved to the <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">Long Island</a> suburb of <a href="/wiki/Rockville_Centre,_New_York" title="Rockville Centre, New York">Rockville Centre</a>. Before tenth grade, Koufax's family moved back to the <a href="/wiki/Bensonhurst,_Brooklyn" title="Bensonhurst, Brooklyn">Bensonhurst</a> section of Brooklyn.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>Koufax attended Brooklyn's <a href="/wiki/Lafayette_High_School_(New_York_City)" title="Lafayette High School (New York City)">Lafayette High School</a>, where he was better known for <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> than for baseball. At the time, school sports were not available because New York's teachers were refusing to supervise extracurricular activities without monetary compensation. As an alternative, Koufax started playing basketball for the <a href="/wiki/Edith_and_Carl_Marks_Jewish_Community_House_of_Bensonhurst" title="Edith and Carl Marks Jewish Community House of Bensonhurst">Edith and Carl Marks Jewish Community House of Bensonhurst</a> local community center team. Eventually, Lafayette had a basketball team; Koufax became team captain in his senior year, and ranked second in his division in scoring, with 165 points in 10 games.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jewishvirtuallibrary.org_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-jewishvirtuallibrary.org-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> In 1951, at the age of 15, Koufax also joined a local youth baseball league known as the "Ice Cream League." He started out as a left-handed catcher before moving to first base. While playing first base for Lafayette High School's baseball team with teammate and friend <a href="/wiki/Fred_Wilpon" title="Fred Wilpon">Fred Wilpon</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> he was spotted by Milt Laurie, the father of two Lafayette teammates and a baseball coach. Laurie recognized that Koufax might be able to pitch, and recruited the 17-year-old Koufax to pitch for the Coney Island Sports League's Parkviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Koufax attended the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cincinnati" title="University of Cincinnati">University of Cincinnati</a> and was a <a href="/wiki/Walk-on_(sports)" title="Walk-on (sports)">walk-on</a> on the freshman basketball team, a complete unknown to coach Ed Jucker.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hickocksports.com_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-hickocksports.com-9">[9]</a></sup> He later earned a partial scholarship. In spring 1954, he made the college baseball <a href="/wiki/Varsity_team" title="Varsity team">varsity team</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> That season, Koufax went 3–1 with a 2.81 <a href="/wiki/Earned_run_average" title="Earned run average">ERA</a>, 51 <a href="/wiki/Strikeout" title="Strikeout">strikeouts</a> and 30 <a href="/wiki/Base_on_balls" title="Base on balls">walks</a>, in 32 innings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bill_Zinser" title="Bill Zinser">Bill Zinser</a>, a scout for the Brooklyn Dodgers, sent the Dodgers front office a glowing report that apparently was filed and forgotten.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>After trying out with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_Giants_(NL)" title="New York Giants (NL)">New York Giants</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Polo_Grounds" title="Polo Grounds">Polo Grounds</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Koufax did the same for the <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh_Pirates" title="Pittsburgh Pirates">Pittsburgh Pirates</a> at <a href="/wiki/Forbes_Field" title="Forbes Field">Forbes Field</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> During his Pirates tryout, Koufax's fastball broke the thumb of <a href="/wiki/Sam_Narron_(catcher)" title="Sam Narron (catcher)">Sam Narron</a>, the team's bullpen coach. <a href="/wiki/Branch_Rickey" title="Branch Rickey">Branch Rickey</a>, then the <a href="/wiki/General_manager_(baseball)" title="General manager (baseball)">general manager</a> of the Pirates, told his scout <a href="/wiki/Clyde_Sukeforth" title="Clyde Sukeforth">Clyde Sukeforth</a> that Koufax had the "greatest arm [he had] ever seen."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> The Pirates, however, failed to offer Koufax a contract until after he was already committed to the Dodgers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Dodgers scout <a href="/wiki/Al_Campanis" title="Al Campanis">Al Campanis</a> heard about Koufax from a local sporting goods store owner. After seeing Koufax pitch for Lafayette, Campanis invited him to an <a href="/wiki/Ebbets_Field" title="Ebbets Field">Ebbets Field</a> tryout. With Dodgers manager <a href="/wiki/Walter_Alston" title="Walter Alston">Walter Alston</a> and scouting director <a href="/wiki/Fresco_Thompson" title="Fresco Thompson">Fresco Thompson</a> watching, Campanis assumed the hitter's stance while Koufax started throwing. Campanis later said, "There are two times in my life the hair on my arms has stood up: The first time I saw the ceiling of the <a href="/wiki/Sistine_Chapel" title="Sistine Chapel">Sistine Chapel</a> and the second time, I saw Sandy Koufax throw a fastball."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The Dodgers signed Koufax for a $6,000 ($54,000 today) salary, with a $14,000 ($125,000 today) <a href="/wiki/Signing_bonus" title="Signing bonus">signing bonus</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Koufax planned to use the money as tuition to finish his university education, if his baseball career failed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Professional_career">Professional career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sandy_Koufax&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Professional career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years_.281955.E2.80.9360.29">Early years (1955–60)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sandy_Koufax&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early years (1955–60)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Because Koufax's signing bonus was greater than $4,000 ($36,000 today), he was known as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bonus_rule" title="Bonus rule">bonus baby</a>. This forced the Dodgers to keep him on the major league roster for at least two years before he could be sent to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Minor_league_baseball" title="Minor league baseball">minors</a>. To make room for him, the Dodgers optioned their future <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Baseball_Hall_of_Fame" title="Baseball Hall of Fame">Hall of Fame</a> manager, <a href="/wiki/Tommy_Lasorda" title="Tommy Lasorda">Tommy Lasorda</a>, to the <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Royals" title="Montreal Royals">Montreal Royals</a> of the <a href="/wiki/International_League" title="International League">International League</a>. Lasorda would later joke that it took Koufax to keep him off the Dodger pitching staff.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>Koufax made his major league debut on June 24, <a href="/wiki/1955_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1955 Major League Baseball season">1955</a> against the <a href="/wiki/1955_Milwaukee_Braves_season" title="1955 Milwaukee Braves season">Milwaukee Braves</a>, with the Dodgers trailing 7–1 in the fifth inning. <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Logan_(baseball)" title="Johnny Logan (baseball)">Johnny Logan</a>, the first batter Koufax faced, hit a bloop single. <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Mathews" title="Eddie Mathews">Eddie Mathews</a> bunted, and Koufax threw the ball into center field. Koufax walked <a href="/wiki/Hank_Aaron" title="Hank Aaron">Hank Aaron</a> on four pitches to load the bases, then struck out <a href="/wiki/Bobby_Thomson" title="Bobby Thomson">Bobby Thomson</a> on a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Full_count" title="Full count">full count</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:127px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cincinnati_Redlegs_at_Brooklyn_Dodgers_1955-08-27_(ticket).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="666" data-file-width="348" height="239" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Cincinnati_Redlegs_at_Brooklyn_Dodgers_1955-08-27_%28ticket%29.jpg/125px-Cincinnati_Redlegs_at_Brooklyn_Dodgers_1955-08-27_%28ticket%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Cincinnati_Redlegs_at_Brooklyn_Dodgers_1955-08-27_%28ticket%29.jpg/188px-Cincinnati_Redlegs_at_Brooklyn_Dodgers_1955-08-27_%28ticket%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Cincinnati_Redlegs_at_Brooklyn_Dodgers_1955-08-27_%28ticket%29.jpg/250px-Cincinnati_Redlegs_at_Brooklyn_Dodgers_1955-08-27_%28ticket%29.jpg 2x" width="125"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cincinnati_Redlegs_at_Brooklyn_Dodgers_1955-08-27_(ticket).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A ticket from the game where Koufax earned his first career win.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Koufax's first start was on July 6.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> He lasted only <span class="nowrap"> </span><span class="frac nowrap">4<span class="visualhide"> </span><sup>2</sup>⁄<sub>3</sub></span> innings, giving up eight walks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> He did not start again for almost two months, but on August 27, Koufax threw a two-hit, 7–0 <a href="/wiki/Complete_game" title="Complete game">complete game</a> <a href="/wiki/Shutouts_in_baseball" title="Shutouts in baseball">shutout</a> against the <a href="/wiki/1955_Cincinnati_Redlegs_season" title="1955 Cincinnati Redlegs season">Cincinnati Reds</a> for his first major league win.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Koufax made only 12 appearances in 1955, pitching <span class="nowrap"> </span><span class="frac nowrap">41<span class="visualhide"> </span><sup>2</sup>⁄<sub>3</sub></span> innings and walking almost as many men (28) as he struck out (30). His only other win in 1955 was also a shutout.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the fall, he enrolled in the <a href="/wiki/Columbia_University_School_of_General_Studies" title="Columbia University School of General Studies">Columbia University School of General Studies</a>, which offered night classes in architecture. The <a href="/wiki/1955_Brooklyn_Dodgers_season" title="1955 Brooklyn Dodgers season">Dodgers</a> won the <a href="/wiki/1955_World_Series" title="1955 World Series">1955 World Series</a> for the first title in franchise history, but Koufax did not appear in the series. After the final out of Game Seven, Koufax drove to Columbia to attend class.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>The year 1956 was not very different from 1955 for Koufax. Despite the blazing speed of his fastball, Koufax continued to struggle with his control.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> He saw little work, pitching only 58.7 innings with a 4.91 ERA, 29 walks and 30 strikeouts. When Koufax allowed baserunners, he was rarely permitted to finish the inning. Teammate <a href="/wiki/Joe_Pignatano" title="Joe Pignatano">Joe Pignatano</a> said that, as soon as Koufax threw a couple of balls in a row, Alston would signal for a replacement to start warming up in the bullpen. <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson" title="Jackie Robinson">Jackie Robinson</a>, in his final season, clashed with Alston on Koufax's usage. Robinson saw that Koufax was talented and had flashes of brilliance, and objected to Koufax being benched for weeks at a time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<p>To prepare for the <a href="/wiki/1957_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1957 Major League Baseball season">1957</a> season, the <a href="/wiki/1957_Brooklyn_Dodgers_season" title="1957 Brooklyn Dodgers season">Dodgers</a> sent Koufax to <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> to play winter ball. On May 15, the restriction on sending Koufax down to the minors was lifted. Alston gave him a chance to justify his place on the major league roster by giving him the next day's start. Facing the <a href="/wiki/1957_Chicago_Cubs_season" title="1957 Chicago Cubs season">Chicago Cubs</a> at <a href="/wiki/Wrigley_Field" title="Wrigley Field">Wrigley Field</a>, Koufax struck out 13 while pitching his first complete game in almost two years. For the first time in his career, he was in the starting rotation, but only for two weeks. Despite winning three of his next five with a 2.90 ERA, Koufax didn't get another start for 45 days. In that start, he struck out 11 in seven innings, but got a no-decision. On September 29, Koufax became the last man ever to pitch for the Brooklyn Dodgers before their move to Los Angeles, by throwing an inning of relief in the final game of the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup></p>
<p>Over the next three seasons, Koufax was in and out of the Dodger starting rotation due to injuries. In 1958, he began 7–3, but sprained his ankle in a collision at first base, finishing the season at 11–11 and leading the NL in wild pitches. In June 1959, Koufax set the record for a night game with 16 strikeouts. On August 31, 1959, he surpassed his career high with 18 strikeouts, setting the NL record and tying <a href="/wiki/Bob_Feller" title="Bob Feller">Bob Feller</a>'s major league record for strikeouts in one game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/1959_in_baseball" title="1959 in baseball">1959</a>, the Dodgers won a close pennant race against the <a href="/wiki/1959_Milwaukee_Braves_season" title="1959 Milwaukee Braves season">Braves</a> and the <a href="/wiki/1959_San_Francisco_Giants_season" title="1959 San Francisco Giants season">Giants</a>, then beat the <a href="/wiki/1959_Chicago_White_Sox_season" title="1959 Chicago White Sox season">Chicago White Sox</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1959_World_Series" title="1959 World Series">World Series</a>. Koufax pitched two perfect relief innings in the Series opener, though they came after the Dodgers were already behind 11–0. Alston gave him the start in the fifth game, at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Coliseum" title="Los Angeles Coliseum">Los Angeles Coliseum</a> in front of 92,706 fans. Koufax allowed only one run in seven innings, but lost the 1–0 game when <a href="/wiki/Nellie_Fox" title="Nellie Fox">Nellie Fox</a> scored on a double play. Returning to Chicago, the Dodgers won the sixth game and the Series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<p>In early <a href="/wiki/1960_in_baseball" title="1960 in baseball">1960</a>, Koufax asked Dodgers GM <a href="/wiki/Buzzie_Bavasi" title="Buzzie Bavasi">Buzzie Bavasi</a> to trade him because he wasn't getting enough playing time. By the end of <a href="/wiki/1960_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="1960 Los Angeles Dodgers season">1960</a>, after going 8–13, Koufax was thinking about quitting baseball to devote himself to an <a href="/wiki/Electronics" title="Electronics">electronics</a> business that he'd invested in. After the last game of the season, he threw his gloves and spikes into the trash. Nobe Kawano, the clubhouse supervisor, retrieved the equipment to return to Koufax the following year (or to somebody else if Koufax did not return to play).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Domination_.281961.E2.80.9364.29">Domination (1961–64)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sandy_Koufax&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Domination (1961–64)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1961_season">1961 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sandy_Koufax&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1961 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sandy_Koufax_1961.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="375" data-file-width="311" height="217" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Sandy_Koufax_1961.png/180px-Sandy_Koufax_1961.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Sandy_Koufax_1961.png/270px-Sandy_Koufax_1961.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f1/Sandy_Koufax_1961.png 2x" width="180"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sandy_Koufax_1961.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Koufax in 1961.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Koufax tried one more year of baseball and showed up for the 1961 season in better condition than he had in previous years. Years later he recalled, "That winter was when I really started working out. I started running more. I decided I was really going to find out how good I can be."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> During spring training, Dodger scout Kenny Myers discovered a hitch in Koufax's windup: he'd rear back so far that his vision was obstructed and he couldn't see the target.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>A day later, Koufax was pitching for the "B team" in <a href="/wiki/Orlando,_Florida" title="Orlando, Florida">Orlando</a>. Teammate <a href="/wiki/Ed_Palmquist" title="Ed Palmquist">Ed Palmquist</a> missed the flight, so Koufax was told he would need to pitch at least seven innings. In the first inning, Koufax walked the bases loaded on 12 straight pitches. Catcher <a href="/wiki/Norm_Sherry" title="Norm Sherry">Norm Sherry</a> advised Koufax to throw slightly less hard in order to improve his control. The advice worked, as Koufax struck out the side, going on to pitch seven no-hit innings.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>It was the beginning of Koufax's breakout season. Posting an 18–13 record for the Dodgers in 1961, Koufax led the league with 269 strikeouts, breaking <a href="/wiki/Christy_Mathewson" title="Christy Mathewson">Christy Mathewson</a>'s 58-year-old NL mark of 267.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Koufax was selected as an All-Star for the first time and made two <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_All-Star_Game" title="Major League Baseball All-Star Game">All-Star Game</a> appearances; MLB held two All-Star games from 1959 through 1962.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sportsdatallc.com_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-sportsdatallc.com-42">[42]</a></sup> He faced only one batter in the 9th inning in the first game, giving up a hit to <a href="/wiki/Al_Kaline" title="Al Kaline">Al Kaline</a> and he pitched two scoreless innings in the second game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1962_season">1962 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sandy_Koufax&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1962 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/1962_in_baseball" title="1962 in baseball">1962</a>, the Dodgers moved from the Los Angeles Coliseum, which had a 250-foot left field line, to pitcher-friendly <a href="/wiki/Dodger_Stadium" title="Dodger Stadium">Dodger Stadium</a>. The new park had a large foul territory and a comparatively poor hitting background. Koufax was an immediate beneficiary of the change, lowering his home ERA from 4.29 to 1.75.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> On June 30 against the expansion <a href="/wiki/New_York_Mets" title="New York Mets">New York Mets</a>, Koufax threw his first no-hitter. In the first inning of that game, Koufax struck out three batters on nine pitches to become the sixth National League pitcher and the 11th pitcher in Major League history to accomplish a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pitchers_who_struck_out_three_batters_on_nine_pitches" title="Pitchers who struck out three batters on nine pitches">nine-pitch/three-strikeout half-inning</a>. With the no-hitter, a 4-2 record, 73 strikeouts, and a 1.23 ERA for June, he was named <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Player_of_the_Month" title="Player of the Month">Player of the Month</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9pitch9strike_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-9pitch9strike-46">[46]</a></sup> It would be the only time in his career he earned this distinction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1962_Bell_Brand_Sandy_Koufax.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1065" data-file-width="733" height="320" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/1962_Bell_Brand_Sandy_Koufax.jpg/220px-1962_Bell_Brand_Sandy_Koufax.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/1962_Bell_Brand_Sandy_Koufax.jpg/330px-1962_Bell_Brand_Sandy_Koufax.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/1962_Bell_Brand_Sandy_Koufax.jpg/440px-1962_Bell_Brand_Sandy_Koufax.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1962_Bell_Brand_Sandy_Koufax.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
1962 <a href="/wiki/Bell_Brand_Snack_Foods" title="Bell Brand Snack Foods">Bell Brand</a> Sandy Koufax</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Koufax had his strong season despite an injured pitching hand. While batting in April, Koufax had been jammed by a pitch from <a href="/wiki/Earl_Francis" title="Earl Francis">Earl Francis</a>. A numbness developed in Koufax's index finger on his left hand, and the finger became cold and white. Koufax was pitching better than ever, however, so he ignored the problem, hoping that the condition would clear up. By July, though, his entire hand was becoming numb and he was unable to complete some games. In a start in Cincinnati, his finger split open after one inning. A vascular specialist determined that Koufax had a crushed artery in his palm. Ten days of experimental medicine successfully reopened the artery. Koufax finally was able to pitch again in September, when the team was locked in a tight pennant race with the Giants. But after the long layoff, Koufax was ineffective in three appearances as the Giants caught the Dodgers at the end of the regular season, forcing a three-game playoff.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<p>The night before the National League playoffs began, Manager <a href="/wiki/Walter_Alston" title="Walter Alston">Walter Alston</a> asked Koufax if he could start the first game the next day. With an overworked pitching staff, there was no one else, as <a href="/wiki/Don_Drysdale" title="Don Drysdale">Don Drysdale</a> and <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Podres" title="Johnny Podres">Johnny Podres</a> had pitched the prior two days. Koufax obliged. Koufax later said, "I had nothing at all." He was knocked out in the second inning, after giving up home runs to Hall of Famer <a href="/wiki/Willie_Mays" title="Willie Mays">Willie Mays</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jim_Davenport" title="Jim Davenport">Jim Davenport</a>. After winning the second game of the series, the Dodgers blew a 4–2 lead in the ninth inning of the deciding third game, losing the pennant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1963_season">1963 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sandy_Koufax&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 1963 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 1963, Major League Baseball expanded the <a href="/wiki/Strike_zone" title="Strike zone">strike zone</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> Compared to the previous season, National League walks fell 13 percent, strikeouts increased six percent, the league batting average fell from .261 to .245, and runs fell 15 percent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> Koufax, who had reduced his walks allowed per nine innings to 3.4 in 1961 and 2.8 in 1962, reduced his walk rate further to 1.7 in 1963, which ranked fifth in the league.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbref-skoufax_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbref-skoufax-3">[3]</a></sup> The top pitchers of the era – <a href="/wiki/Don_Drysdale" title="Don Drysdale">Don Drysdale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Marichal" title="Juan Marichal">Juan Marichal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Bunning" title="Jim Bunning">Jim Bunning</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bob_Gibson" title="Bob Gibson">Bob Gibson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warren_Spahn" title="Warren Spahn">Warren Spahn</a>, and above all Koufax – significantly reduced the walks-given-up-to-batters-faced ratio for 1963, and subsequent years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>On May 11, Koufax <a href="/wiki/No-hitter" title="No-hitter">no-hit</a> the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Giants" title="San Francisco Giants">San Francisco Giants</a> 8-0, besting future Hall of Fame pitcher <a href="/wiki/Juan_Marichal" title="Juan Marichal">Juan Marichal</a>—himself a no-hit pitcher a month later, on June 15. Koufax carried a <a href="/wiki/Perfect_game" title="Perfect game">perfect game</a> into the eighth inning against the powerful <a href="/wiki/1963_San_Francisco_Giants_season" title="1963 San Francisco Giants season">Giants</a> lineup, including future Hall of Famers Willie Mays, <a href="/wiki/Willie_McCovey" title="Willie McCovey">Willie McCovey</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Orlando_Cepeda" title="Orlando Cepeda">Orlando Cepeda</a>. He walked <a href="/wiki/Ed_Bailey" title="Ed Bailey">Ed Bailey</a> on a 3-and-2 pitch in the 8th, and pinch-hitter McCovey on four pitches in the 9th, before closing out the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> As the Dodgers won the pennant, Koufax won the pitchers' <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Triple_Crown" title="Major League Baseball Triple Crown">Triple Crown</a>, leading the league in wins (25), strikeouts (306) and ERA (1.88). Koufax threw 11 shutouts, setting a new record for shutouts by a left-handed pitcher that stands to this day (the previous record of 9 shutouts had been held by Babe Ruth for nearly 50 years). Only <a href="/wiki/Bob_Gibson" title="Bob Gibson">Bob Gibson</a>, a right-hander, has thrown more shutouts (13) since, and that was in 1968, "the year of the pitcher."</p>
<p>Koufax won the NL <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MLB_Most_Valuable_Player_award" title="MLB Most Valuable Player award">MVP Award</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Hickok_Belt" title="Hickok Belt">Hickok Belt</a>, and was the first-ever unanimous selection for the <a href="/wiki/Cy_Young_Award" title="Cy Young Award">Cy Young Award</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hickokbelt_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-hickokbelt-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>Facing the <a href="/wiki/1963_New_York_Yankees_season" title="1963 New York Yankees season">Yankees</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1963_World_Series" title="1963 World Series">1963 World Series</a>, Koufax beat <a href="/wiki/Whitey_Ford" title="Whitey Ford">Whitey Ford</a> 5–2 in Game 1 and struck out 15 batters-including the first 5, breaking <a href="/wiki/Carl_Erskine" title="Carl Erskine">Carl Erskine</a>'s decade-old record of 14 (Gibson would break Koufax's record by striking out 17 <a href="/wiki/1968_Detroit_Tigers_season" title="1968 Detroit Tigers season">Detroit Tigers</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1968_World_Series" title="1968 World Series">1968 World Series</a> opener). After seeing Koufax's Game 1 performance, <a href="/wiki/Yogi_Berra" title="Yogi Berra">Yogi Berra</a> said, "I can see how he won 25 games. What I don't understand is how he lost five,"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> to which <a href="/wiki/Maury_Wills" title="Maury Wills">Maury Wills</a> responded, "He didn't. We lost them for him."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> In Game 4, Koufax completed the Dodgers' series sweep with a 2–1 victory over Ford, clinching the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Series_MVP_Award" title="World Series MVP Award">Series MVP Award</a> for his performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1964_season">1964 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sandy_Koufax&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 1964 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Koufax's <a href="/wiki/1964_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1964 Major League Baseball season">1964</a> season started with great expectations. On April 18, he struck out three batters on nine pitches in the third inning of a 3–0 loss to the <a href="/wiki/1964_Cincinnati_Reds_season" title="1964 Cincinnati Reds season">Cincinnati Reds</a>, becoming the only National League pitcher to have two <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pitchers_who_struck_out_three_batters_on_nine_pitches" title="Pitchers who struck out three batters on nine pitches">nine-pitch/three-strikeout half-innings</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9pitch9strike_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-9pitch9strike-46">[46]</a></sup> On April 22, however, he felt something "let go" in his arm. Koufax ended up getting three <a href="/wiki/Cortisone" title="Cortisone">cortisone</a> shots for his sore elbow, and missed three starts.</p>
<p>On June 4, playing at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Connie_Mack_Stadium" title="Connie Mack Stadium">Connie Mack Stadium</a> against the <a href="/wiki/1964_Philadelphia_Phillies_season" title="1964 Philadelphia Phillies season">Phillies</a>, Koufax <a href="/wiki/Base_on_balls" title="Base on balls">walked</a> <a href="/wiki/Dick_Allen" title="Dick Allen">Richie Allen</a> on a very close full-count pitch in the fourth inning. Allen, who was thrown out trying to steal second, was the only Phillie to reach base that day. With his third no-hitter in three years, Koufax became only the second pitcher of the modern era (after <a href="/wiki/Bob_Feller" title="Bob Feller">Bob Feller</a>) to pitch three no-hitters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>Koufax jammed his pitching arm in August while diving back to second base to beat a pick-off throw. He managed to pitch and win two more games. However, the morning after his 19th win, a shutout in which he struck out 13 batters, he could not straighten his arm. He was diagnosed by Dodgers' team physician <a href="/wiki/Robert_Kerlan" title="Robert Kerlan">Robert Kerlan</a> with traumatic <a href="/wiki/Arthritis" title="Arthritis">arthritis</a>. With the Dodgers out of the pennant race, the book was closed on Koufax and his 19–5 record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Playing_in_pain_.281965.E2.80.9366.29">Playing in pain (1965–66)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sandy_Koufax&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Playing in pain (1965–66)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1965_season">1965 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sandy_Koufax&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 1965 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The 1965 season brought more obstacles for Koufax. On March 31, the morning after pitching a complete <a href="/wiki/Spring_training" title="Spring training">spring training</a> game, Koufax awoke to find that his entire left arm was <a href="/wiki/Bruise" title="Bruise">black and blue</a> from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hemorrhage" title="Hemorrhage">hemorrhaging</a>. Koufax returned to Los Angeles to consult with Kerlan, who advised Koufax that he would be lucky to be able to pitch once a week. Kerlan also told Koufax that he would eventually lose full use of his arm. Koufax agreed not to throw at all between games—a resolution that lasted only one start. To get himself through the games he pitched in, Koufax resorted to Empirin with <a href="/wiki/Codeine" title="Codeine">codeine</a> for the pain, which he took every night and sometimes during the fifth inning. He also took <a href="/wiki/Phenylbutazone" title="Phenylbutazone">Butazolidin</a> for inflammation, applied <a href="/wiki/Capsaicin" title="Capsaicin">capsaicin</a>-based Capsolin ointment (called "atomic balm" by baseball players) before each game, and soaked his arm in a tub of ice afterwards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>Despite the constant pain in his pitching elbow, Koufax pitched 335⅔ innings and led the <a href="/wiki/1965_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="1965 Los Angeles Dodgers season">Dodgers</a> to another pennant. He finished the year by winning his second pitchers' Triple Crown, leading the league in wins (26), ERA (2.04) and strikeouts (382; the highest modern day total at the time. <a href="/wiki/Nolan_Ryan" title="Nolan Ryan">Nolan Ryan</a> struck out 383 batters in <a href="/wiki/1973_in_baseball" title="1973 in baseball">1973</a>). Koufax captured his second unanimous Cy Young Award. Koufax held batters to 5.79 hits per nine innings, and allowed the fewest base runners per 9 innings in any season ever: 7.83, breaking his own record (set two years earlier) of 7.96. Koufax had 11-game winning streaks in both 1964 and 1965.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbref-skoufax_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-bbref-skoufax-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Perfection">Perfection</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sandy_Koufax&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Perfection">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Koufax%27s_perfect_game" title="Sandy Koufax's perfect game">Sandy Koufax's perfect game</a></div>
<p>On September 9, 1965, Koufax became the sixth pitcher of the modern era, and eighth overall, to throw a perfect game, the first by a left-hander since 1880. The game was Koufax's fourth no-hitter, setting a Major League record (subsequently broken by <a href="/wiki/Nolan_Ryan" title="Nolan Ryan">Nolan Ryan</a>). Koufax struck out 14 batters, at the time the most recorded in a perfect game (now tied by <a href="/wiki/Matt_Cain" title="Matt Cain">Matt Cain</a>). The game also featured a quality performance by the opposing pitcher, <a href="/wiki/Bob_Hendley" title="Bob Hendley">Bob Hendley</a> of the <a href="/wiki/1965_Chicago_Cubs_season" title="1965 Chicago Cubs season">Cubs</a>. Hendley pitched a one-hitter and allowed only two batters to reach base. Both pitchers had no-hitters intact until the seventh inning.</p>
<p>This remains the only nine-inning major league game where the teams combined for just one hit. The game's only run, scored by the Dodgers, was <a href="/wiki/Earned_run" title="Earned run">unearned</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-baseballlibrary_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-baseballlibrary-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> The Dodger run was scored without a recorded at bat—<a href="/wiki/Lou_Johnson" title="Lou Johnson">Lou Johnson</a> walked, reached second on a sacrifice bunt, stole third, and scored when the throw to get him out at third went wild.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Series_and_Yom_Kippur">World Series and Yom Kippur</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sandy_Koufax&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: World Series and Yom Kippur">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Koufax garnered headlines by declining to pitch Game 1 of the <a href="/wiki/1965_World_Series" title="1965 World Series">World Series</a> because of his observance of the Jewish religious holiday of Yom Kippur. This decision garnered national attention as an example of conflict between professional pressures and personal religious beliefs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-yomkippur_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-yomkippur-7">[7]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Don_Drysdale" title="Don Drysdale">Don Drysdale</a> pitched the opener, but was hit hard by the <a href="/wiki/1965_Minnesota_Twins_season" title="1965 Minnesota Twins season">Minnesota Twins</a>.</p>
<p>In Game 2, Koufax pitched six innings, giving up two runs, but the Twins won the Game 5–1 and took an early 2–0 lead in the series. The Dodgers fought back in Games 3 and 4, with wins by <a href="/wiki/Claude_Osteen" title="Claude Osteen">Claude Osteen</a> and Drysdale. With the Series tied at 2 to 2, Koufax pitched a complete game shutout in Game 5 for a 3–2 Dodgers lead as the Series returned to <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Stadium" title="Metropolitan Stadium">Minnesota's Metropolitan Stadium</a> for Game 6. The Twins won Game 6 to force a seventh game. Starting Game 7 on just two days of rest, Koufax pitched through fatigue and arthritic pain. Despite giving up on his curveball early in the game after failing to get it over for strikes in the first two innings and pitching the rest of the game relying almost entirely on fastballs, he threw a three-hit shutout to clinch the Series. The performance earned him his second World Series MVP award. Koufax also won the <a href="/wiki/Hickok_Belt" title="Hickok Belt">Hickok Belt</a> a second time, the first time anyone had won the belt more than once. He was awarded <i><a href="/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a></i> magazine's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sportsman_of_the_Year" title="Sportsman of the Year">Sportsman of the Year</a> award.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbref-skoufax_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-bbref-skoufax-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hickokbelt_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-hickokbelt-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1966_season">1966 season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sandy_Koufax&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 1966 season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Holdout">Holdout</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sandy_Koufax&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Holdout">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>Before the 1966 season began, Koufax and Drysdale met separately with Dodger GM <a href="/wiki/Buzzie_Bavasi" title="Buzzie Bavasi">Buzzie Bavasi</a> to negotiate their contracts for the upcoming year. After Koufax's meeting, he met Drysdale for dinner and complained that Bavasi was using Drysdale against him in the negotiations, asking, "How come you want that much when Drysdale only wants this much?"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> Drysdale responded that Bavasi did the same thing with him, using Koufax against him. Drysdale's first wife, Ginger Drysdale, suggested that they negotiate together to get what they wanted. They demanded $1 million ($7,380,000 today), divided equally over the next three years, or $167,000 ($1,233,000 today) each for each of the next three seasons. Both players were represented by an entertainment lawyer, J. William Hayes, which was unusual during an era when players were not represented by agents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-STT_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-STT-69">[69]</a></sup> At the time, Willie Mays was <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a>'s highest paid player at $125,000 ($923,000 today) per year and multi-year contracts were very unusual.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DP_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-DP-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>Koufax and Drysdale did not report to spring training in February. Instead, they both signed to appear in the movie <i><a href="/wiki/Warning_Shot" title="Warning Shot">Warning Shot</a></i>, starring <a href="/wiki/David_Janssen" title="David Janssen">David Janssen</a>. Drysdale was to play a TV commentator and Koufax a <a href="/wiki/Detective" title="Detective">detective</a>. Meanwhile, the Dodgers waged a <a href="/wiki/Public_relations" title="Public relations">public relations</a> battle against them. After four weeks, Koufax gave Drysdale the go-ahead to negotiate new deals for both of them. Koufax ended up getting $125,000 and Drysdale $110,000 ($812,000 today). They rejoined the team in the last week of spring training.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> In April 1966, Kerlan told Koufax it was time to retire and that his arm could not take another season. Koufax kept Kerlan's advice to himself and went out every fourth day to pitch. He ended up pitching 323 innings, a 27–9 record, and a 1.73 ERA. Since then, no left-hander has had more wins, nor a lower ERA, in a season (Phillies pitcher <a href="/wiki/Steve_Carlton" title="Steve Carlton">Steve Carlton</a> did match the 27-win mark in 1972). In the final game of the regular season, the Dodgers had to beat the Phillies to win the pennant. In the second game of a doubleheader, Koufax faced <a href="/wiki/Jim_Bunning" title="Jim Bunning">Jim Bunning</a> for the second time that season,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> in a match-up between perfect game winners. Koufax, on two days rest, pitched a complete game, 6–3 victory to clinch the pennant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> He started 41 games (for the second year in a row); only two left-handers started as many games in any season over the ensuing years through 2016.</p>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="Season">Season</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sandy_Koufax&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Season">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h5>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/1966_Los_Angeles_Dodgers_season" title="1966 Los Angeles Dodgers season">Dodgers</a> went on to face the <a href="/wiki/1966_Baltimore_Orioles_season" title="1966 Baltimore Orioles season">Baltimore Orioles</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1966_World_Series" title="1966 World Series">1966 World Series</a>. Game 2 marked Koufax's third start in eight days. Koufax pitched well enough—Baltimore first baseman <a href="/wiki/Boog_Powell" title="Boog Powell">Boog Powell</a> told Koufax's biographer, Jane Leavy, "He might have been hurtin' but he was bringin'"—but three errors by Dodger center fielder <a href="/wiki/Willie_Davis_(baseball)" title="Willie Davis (baseball)">Willie Davis</a> in the fifth inning produced three unearned runs. Baltimore's <a href="/wiki/Jim_Palmer" title="Jim Palmer">Jim Palmer</a> pitched a four-hitter and the Dodgers ended up losing the game 6–0. Alston lifted Koufax at the end of the sixth inning<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> with the idea of getting him extra rest before pitching a potential fifth Series game. It never happened; the Dodgers were swept in four, not scoring a single run in the last three. After the World Series, Koufax announced his retirement due to his arthritic condition on Friday, November 18, 1966.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_overall">Career overall</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sandy_Koufax&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Career overall">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In his 12-season career, Koufax had a 165–87 record with a 2.76 ERA, 2,396 strikeouts, 137 complete games, and 40 shutouts. He was the first pitcher to average fewer than seven <a href="/wiki/Hit_(baseball)" title="Hit (baseball)">hits</a> allowed per nine <a href="/wiki/Innings_pitched" title="Innings pitched">innings pitched</a> in his career (6.79) and to strike out more than nine batters (9.28) per nine innings pitched in his career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> He also became the 2nd pitcher in baseball history to have two games with 18 or more strikeouts, and the first to have eight games with 15 or more strikeouts. In his last ten seasons, from 1957 to 1966, batters hit .203 against Koufax, with a .271 <a href="/wiki/On-base_percentage" title="On-base percentage">on-base percentage</a> and a .315 <a href="/wiki/Slugging_percentage" title="Slugging percentage">slugging average</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<p>Koufax's postseason record is impressive: a 4–3 won-lost record with a 0.95 earned run average, in four World Series. He is on the very short list of pitchers who retired with more career strikeouts than innings pitched. Koufax was selected as an All-Star for six consecutive seasons<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-baseballhall.org_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-baseballhall.org-2">[2]</a></sup> and made seven out of eight All-Star Game appearances those seasons (not selected for 2nd All-Star Game in 1962).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sportsdatallc.com_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-sportsdatallc.com-42">[42]</a></sup> He pitched 6<span class="nowrap"> </span><span class="frac nowrap"><sup>1</sup>⁄<sub>3</sub></span> innings in four All-Star games including being the starting pitcher for 3 innings in the 1966 All-Star Game.</p>
<p>Koufax was the first pitcher to win multiple Cy Young Awards, as well as the first pitcher to win a Cy Young Award by a unanimous vote. He is also the only pitcher to win three Cy Young Awards in the era in which the award was presented to one pitcher across the board, rather than one in each major league, and one of three Dodgers pitchers to win the one-across-the-board Cy Young Award. (The others were <a href="/wiki/Don_Newcombe" title="Don Newcombe">Don Newcombe</a>, the first Cy Young winner in 1956, and <a href="/wiki/Don_Drysdale" title="Don Drysdale">Don Drysdale</a> in 1962.) Each of Koufax's three Cy Young Awards were by unanimous vote.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbref-skoufax_3-4"><a href="#cite_note-bbref-skoufax-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Koufax and Juan Marichal are the only two pitchers in the post-war era (1946-date) to have more than one 25-win season, with each pitcher recording three.</p>
<p>Among NL pitchers with at least 2,000 innings pitched who have debuted since <a href="/wiki/1913_in_baseball" title="1913 in baseball">1913</a>, he has the highest career winning percentage (.655) and had the lowest career ERA (2.76) until surpassed by <a href="/wiki/Tom_Seaver" title="Tom Seaver">Tom Seaver</a>, whose NL career mark is 2.73. While Seaver ended his career with an overall career ERA of 2.86, this included three seasons in the American League. Seaver passed Koufax's record in 1974 when he ended the season with more than 2,000 NL innings and an ERA of 2.47. Koufax is currently second on the list of overall career ERA in the live-ball era, surpassed only by Whitey Ford (2.75). Through 2010, he was first all-time in career strikeouts (ahead of <a href="/wiki/Ken_Holtzman" title="Ken Holtzman">Ken Holtzman</a>), second in wins (behind Holtzman) and ERA (behind <a href="/wiki/Barney_Pelty" title="Barney Pelty">Barney Pelty</a>), and seventh in games pitched (behind <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alan_Levine" title="Alan Levine">Alan Levine</a>) among Jewish major league baseball players.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JML_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-JML-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Pitching_style">Pitching style</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sandy_Koufax&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Pitching style">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:20em; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"I knew every pitch he was going to throw and still I couldn't hit him."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup></p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">—<a href="/wiki/Willie_Mays" title="Willie Mays">Willie Mays</a></cite></div>
<p>Whereas many pitchers throw with a three-quarter or sidearm motion, Koufax threw with a pronounced over-the-top arm action. This may have increased his <a href="/wiki/Velocity" title="Velocity">velocity</a>, but reduced the lateral movement on his pitches, especially movement away from left-handed hitters. Most of his velocity came from his strong legs and back, combined with a high kicking wind-up and long forward stretch toward the plate. Throughout his career, Koufax relied mostly on two pitches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pitches_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-pitches-81">[81]</a></sup> His <a href="/wiki/Four-seam_fastball" title="Four-seam fastball">four-seam fastball</a> gave batters the impression of rising as it approached them, due to underspin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> It not only appeared to move very late but also might move two or three distinct times. His overhand <a href="/wiki/Curveball" title="Curveball">curveball</a>, spun with the middle finger, dropped vertically 12 to 24 inches due to his arm action. <a href="/wiki/Rob_Neyer" title="Rob Neyer">Rob Neyer</a> called it the best curve of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> He also occasionally threw a <a href="/wiki/Changeup" title="Changeup">changeup</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Forkball" title="Forkball">forkball</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pitches_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-pitches-81">[81]</a></sup></p>
<p>At the beginning of his career, Koufax worked with coaches to eliminate his tendency to "tip" pitches (i.e. reveal which pitch was coming due to variations in his wind-up). Late in his career, and especially as his arm problems continued, this variation—usually in the position he held his hands at the top of the wind-up—became even more pronounced. Good hitters could often predict what pitch was coming, but were still unable to hit it.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-playing_career">Post-playing career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sandy_Koufax&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Post-playing career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table style="width: 100px; font-size: 90%; float:right; border: 2px solid #aaa; margin: 0em 1em 0em 0em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align: center;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LAret32.PNG"><img alt="LAret32.PNG" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" height="95" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/LAret32.PNG/95px-LAret32.PNG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/LAret32.PNG/143px-LAret32.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/LAret32.PNG/190px-LAret32.PNG 2x" width="95"/></a></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align: center;">Sandy Koufax's number 32 was <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_retired_numbers" title="List of Major League Baseball retired numbers">retired</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers#Retired_numbers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">Los Angeles Dodgers</a> in 1972.</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In 1967, he signed a 10-year contract with <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_on_NBC" title="Major League Baseball on NBC">NBC</a> for US$1 million ($7,183,000 today) to be a broadcaster on the <i><a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_Game_of_the_Week" title="Major League Baseball Game of the Week">Saturday Game of the Week</a></i>. He quit after six years, just prior to the start of the <a href="/wiki/1973_in_baseball" title="1973 in baseball">1973</a> season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-espn65series_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-espn65series-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>Koufax married Anne Widmark, daughter of movie star <a href="/wiki/Richard_Widmark" title="Richard Widmark">Richard Widmark</a>, in 1969; the couple was divorced in the 1980s. He then remarried and divorced again in the 1990s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-espn65series_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-espn65series-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<p>In his first year of eligibility in <a href="/wiki/1972_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1972 Major League Baseball season">1972</a>, Koufax was elected to the Baseball Hall of Fame, just weeks after his 36th birthday. His election made him the Hall's youngest member ever elected, five months younger than <a href="/wiki/Lou_Gehrig" title="Lou Gehrig">Lou Gehrig</a> upon his election in 1939, though because the 1972 induction ceremony was nearly eight months after the election, Koufax's age at induction was slightly higher than Gehrig's, making Gehrig the youngest player ever inducted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kirbypuckett_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-kirbypuckett-1">[1]</a></sup> On June 4 of that same year, Koufax's uniform number 32 was <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Dodgers#Retired_numbers" title="Los Angeles Dodgers">retired</a> alongside those of Dodger greats <a href="/wiki/Roy_Campanella" title="Roy Campanella">Roy Campanella</a> (39) and Jackie Robinson (42).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Dodgers hired Koufax to be a minor league pitching coach in <a href="/wiki/1979_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1979 Major League Baseball season">1979</a>. He resigned in <a href="/wiki/1990_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1990 Major League Baseball season">1990</a>, saying he wasn't earning his keep, but most observers blamed it on his uneasy relationship with manager Tommy Lasorda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> Koufax returned to the Dodger organization in <a href="/wiki/2004_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="2004 Major League Baseball season">2004</a> when the Dodgers were sold to <a href="/wiki/Frank_McCourt_(executive)" title="Frank McCourt (executive)">Frank McCourt</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-baseballlibrary_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-baseballlibrary-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:232px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sandy_Koufax_2014.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2071" data-file-width="2120" height="225" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Sandy_Koufax_2014.jpg/230px-Sandy_Koufax_2014.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Sandy_Koufax_2014.jpg/345px-Sandy_Koufax_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Sandy_Koufax_2014.jpg/460px-Sandy_Koufax_2014.jpg 2x" width="230"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sandy_Koufax_2014.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Koufax at the 2014 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BBWAA" title="BBWAA">BBWAA</a> dinner</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/1999_Major_League_Baseball_season" title="1999 Major League Baseball season">1999</a>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Sporting_News" title="The Sporting News">The Sporting News</a></i> placed Koufax at number 26 on its list of "Baseball's 100 Greatest Players."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> That same year, he was named as one of the 30 players on the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_All-Century_Team" title="Major League Baseball All-Century Team">Major League Baseball All-Century Team</a>. Although he rarely makes public appearances, he went to <a href="/wiki/Turner_Field" title="Turner Field">Turner Field</a> in <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a> for the introduction ceremony before Game 2 of the <a href="/wiki/1999_World_Series" title="1999 World Series">1999 World Series</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> Koufax threw out a ceremonial first pitch at opening day 2008 at Dodger Stadium, to help commemorate the Dodgers' 50th Anniversary in Los Angeles.</p>
<p>Koufax was the final player chosen in the inaugural <a href="/wiki/Israel_Baseball_League" title="Israel Baseball League">Israel Baseball League</a> draft in April 2007. Koufax, 71, was picked by the <a href="/wiki/Modi%27in_Miracle" title="Modi'in Miracle">Modi'in Miracle</a>. "His selection is a tribute to the esteem with which he is held by everyone associated with this league", said <a href="/wiki/Art_Shamsky" title="Art Shamsky">Art Shamsky</a>, who managed the Miracle. "It's been 41 years between starts for him. If he's rested and ready to take the mound again, we want him on our team." Koufax declined to join the Miracle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup></p>
<p>Currently, Koufax serves as a member of the advisory board of the <a href="/wiki/Baseball_Assistance_Team" title="Baseball Assistance Team">Baseball Assistance Team</a>, a 501(c)(3) non-profit organization dedicated to helping former Major League, Minor League, and Negro League players through financial and medical difficulties.</p>
<p>On January 23, 2013 the Dodgers hired Koufax as a Special Advisor to team Chairman <a href="/wiki/Mark_Walter" title="Mark Walter">Mark Walter</a>. Koufax worked with the pitchers during spring training and will consult during the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> On April 1, 2013, Koufax threw out the first pitch during ceremonies at Dodger Stadium.</p>
<p>On July 14, 2015, before the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2015_MLB_All-Star_Game" title="2015 MLB All-Star Game">2015 MLB All-Star Game</a> in Cincinnati, Koufax was introduced as one of the four best living players (as selected by the fans of major league baseball), along with <a href="/wiki/Willie_Mays" title="Willie Mays">Willie Mays</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hank_Aaron" title="Hank Aaron">Hank Aaron</a> and <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Bench" title="Johnny Bench">Johnny Bench</a>. He threw the ceremonial first pitch to Bench from in front of the base of the mound.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Acting_roles">Acting roles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sandy_Koufax&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Acting roles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Koufax appeared on television from 1959 through 1962. He was cast as Ben Cassidy in the 1959 episode "Too Smart to Live" of the <a href="/wiki/Broadcast_syndication" title="Broadcast syndication">syndicated</a> <a href="/wiki/Western_(genre)" title="Western (genre)">western</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Television_series" title="Television series">series</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Shotgun_Slade" title="Shotgun Slade">Shotgun Slade</a></i>, starring <a href="/wiki/Scott_Brady" title="Scott Brady">Scott Brady</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imdb_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-imdb-94">[94]</a></sup> In 1960, he played the role of "Johnny" in the episode <i>Impasse</i> of the <a href="/wiki/American_Broadcasting_Company" title="American Broadcasting Company">ABC</a>/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Warner_Brothers" title="Warner Brothers">Warner Brothers</a> western series, <i><a href="/wiki/Colt_.45_(TV_series)" title="Colt .45 (TV series)">Colt .45</a></i>, with <a href="/wiki/Donald_May" title="Donald May">Donald May</a> as Sam Colt, Jr.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> He made minor appearances in two other ABC/WB productions, <i><a href="/wiki/77_Sunset_Strip" title="77 Sunset Strip">77 Sunset Strip</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Bourbon_Street_Beat" title="Bourbon Street Beat">Bourbon Street Beat</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imdb_94-1"><a href="#cite_note-imdb-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>Koufax also appeared as himself along with several Dodger teammates in an episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Mister_Ed" title="Mister Ed">Mister Ed</a></i> entitled "Leo Durocher Meets Mister Ed" in September 1963.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p>
<p>Koufax portrayed himself on <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Dennis_the_Menace_(1959_TV_series)" title="Dennis the Menace (1959 TV series)">Dennis the Menace</a></i> in the 1962 episode <i>Dennis and the Dodger</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> He also appeared as himself on <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>'s detective series, <i><a href="/wiki/Michael_Shayne" title="Michael Shayne">Michael Shayne</a></i> in the 1961 episode entitled "Strike Out".</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="White_House_recognition">White House recognition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sandy_Koufax&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: White House recognition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:JAHM_2010.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="302" data-file-width="495" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/JAHM_2010.jpg/220px-JAHM_2010.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/JAHM_2010.jpg/330px-JAHM_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/JAHM_2010.jpg/440px-JAHM_2010.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:JAHM_2010.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Sandy Koufax (center of first row) at first White House reception for <a href="/wiki/Jewish_American_Heritage_Month" title="Jewish American Heritage Month">Jewish American Heritage Month</a>, May 27, 2010. At Koufax's right are Vice President <a href="/wiki/Joe_Biden" title="Joe Biden">Joe Biden</a> and First Lady <a href="/wiki/Michelle_Obama" title="Michelle Obama">Michelle Obama</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On May 27, 2010, Koufax was included among a group of prominent Jewish Americans at the first White House reception in honor of <a href="/wiki/Jewish_American_Heritage_Month" title="Jewish American Heritage Month">Jewish American Heritage Month</a>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._President" title="U.S. President">U.S. President</a> <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> recognized how well-known Koufax's decision not to play on the Jewish holy day of Yom Kippur was in a humorous mention in his welcome remarks. Saying that he had "something in common" with Koufax, President Obama continued: "He can't pitch on <a href="/wiki/Yom_Kippur" title="Yom Kippur">Yom Kippur</a>. I can't pitch."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JAHM_98-0"><a href="#cite_note-JAHM-98">[98]</a></sup> The President also directly acknowledged the high esteem in which Koufax is held:</p>
<dl>
<dd>"This is a pretty fancy ... pretty distinguished group", he said of the invited guests, which included members of the House and Senate, two justices of the Supreme Court, Olympic athletes, entrepreneurs, Rabbinical scholars, "and Sandy Koufax." The mention of his name brought the biggest cheer at the event.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JAHM_98-1"><a href="#cite_note-JAHM-98">[98]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sandy_Koufax&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

Boxerman, McFarland, 2010, <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0786428287">ISBN 0-7864-2828-7</a></li>
<li><i><a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=or8LOAAACAAJ" rel="nofollow">The Baseball Talmud: The Definitive Position-by-Position Ranking of Baseball's Chosen Players</a></i>, Howard Megdal, Collins, 2009, <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0061558435">ISBN 0-06-155843-5</a></li>
<li><i><a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=irG7GQAACAAJ" rel="nofollow">The New Big Book of Jewish Baseball: An Illustrated Encyclopedia &amp; Anecdotal History</a></i>, Peter S. Horvitz, Joachim Horvitz, Perseus Distribution Services, 2007, <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1561718211">ISBN 1-56171-821-1</a></li>
<li><a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=qJEQTaE7JEAC" rel="nofollow"><i>Jews and Baseball: Entering the American mainstream, 1871–1948</i></a>, Burton Alan Boxerman, Benita W. Boxerman, McFarland, 2006, <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0786428287">ISBN 0-7864-2828-7</a></li>
<li><i><a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=9ZzxydPInwgC" rel="nofollow">The Big Book of Jewish Baseball: An Illustrated Encyclopedia &amp; Anecdotal History</a></i>, Peter S. Horvitz, Joachim Horvitz, SP Books, 2001, <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1561719730">ISBN 1-56171-973-0</a></li>
<li><i><a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=0-BMAAAACAAJ" rel="nofollow">The Jewish Baseball Hall of Fame: a Who's Who of Baseball Stars</a></i>, Erwin Lynn, Shapolsky Publishers, 1986, <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0933503172">ISBN 0-933503-17-2</a></li>
<li><i><a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=G2o8AAAACAAJ" rel="nofollow">Jewish Baseball Stars</a></i>, Harold Uriel Ribalow, Meir Z. Ribalow, Hippocrene Books, 1984, <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0882548980">ISBN 0-88254-898-0</a></li>
<li>"Sandy Koufax: Pitcher Nonpareil and Perfect Gentleman". In <i>American Jews and America's Game: Voices of a Growing Legacy in Baseball</i>, <a href="/wiki/Larry_Ruttman" title="Larry Ruttman">Larry Ruttman</a>, University of Nebraska Press, 2013, <a class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn" href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780803264755">ISBN 978-0-8032-6475-5</a>. This chapter in Ruttman's history discusses Koufax's American, Jewish, baseball, and life experiences from youth to the present.</li>
</ul>

<li>2011: <a href="/wiki/Justin_Verlander" title="Justin Verlander">Verlander</a></li>
<li>2012: <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Cabrera" title="Miguel Cabrera">Cabrera</a></li>
<li>2013: <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Cabrera" title="Miguel Cabrera">Cabrera</a></li>
<li>2014: <a href="/wiki/Clayton_Kershaw" title="Clayton Kershaw">Kershaw</a></li>
<li>2015: <a href="/wiki/Josh_Donaldson" title="Josh Donaldson">Donaldson</a></li>
<li>2016: <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Altuve" title="José Altuve">Altuve</a></li>
</ul>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
